{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01CLrAQCkQxo5DarpgbKFpxD","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# SkillX Refine Protocol v0.1\n     2→\n     3→- **Project:** `projects/multi-agent-protocol-design`\n     4→- **Date:** 2026-03-23\n     5→- **Role:** multi-round bounded refine protocol for `C4` in the SkillX / SkillsBench experiment line\n     6→- **Status:** planning draft for the first controlled refine stage\n     7→\n     8→---\n     9→\n    10→## 1. Why this document exists\n    11→\n    12→The current SkillX experiment already defines:\n    13→- `C0` — no skill\n    14→- `C1` — original skill\n    15→- `C2` — SkillX minimal rewrite\n    16→- `C3` — SkillX minimal rewrite + agent-derived expansion\n    17→- optional later `C4` — refined variant\n    18→\n    19→But `C4` was previously under-specified.\n    20→\n    21→The important correction is:\n    22→\n    23→> **`C4` should run as a multi-round autoresearch refine loop, but under a frozen refine protocol.**\n    24→\n    25→In other words:\n    26→- the **protocol** is fixed for the duration of the experiment,\n    27→- but the **execution of that protocol** is explicitly multi-round.\n    28→\n    29→This preserves both:\n    30→- the scientific interpretability of the benchmark, and\n    31→- the actual value proposition of autoresearch / self-refine / self-evolve style methods.\n    32→\n    33→---\n    34→\n    35→## 2. Core clarification\n    36→\n    37→Two design choices were previously easy to conflate:\n    38→\n    39→1. **Should the refine protocol be frozen or evolving?**\n    40→2. **Should the refine process itself be single-round or multi-round?**\n    41→\n    42→These are not the same question.\n    43→\n    44→### 2.1 Policy for v0.1\n    45→For the current SkillX benchmark:\n    46→- the **refine protocol should be frozen**\n    47→- the **refine execution should be multi-round by default**\n    48→\n    49→### 2.2 Why this matters\n    50→If we freeze the protocol but allow multiple rounds, we still get:\n    51→- iterative diagnosis,\n    52→- accumulation of evidence,\n    53→- round-to-round skill improvement,\n    54→- and a meaningful role for memory.\n    55→\n    56→But we avoid mixing in a second harder-to-interpret question:\n    57→- whether the system is also inventing a better refine protocol while it is optimizing the skill.\n    58→\n    59→---\n    60→\n    61→## 3. What `C4` means in v0.1\n    62→\n    63→`C4` is:\n    64→\n    65→> a **bounded multi-round refinement loop** that starts from `C3`, consumes tune-split evidence, and outputs a final refined skill candidate for held-out evaluation.\n    66→\n    67→### 3.1 Short definition\n    68→- **starting artifact:** `C3`\n    69→- **refiner:** Pi-AutoResearch (or equivalent bounded refiner)\n    70→- **execution style:** multi-round\n    71→- **protocol status:** frozen\n    72→- **evidence source:** tune split only\n    73→- **evaluation claim:** held-out eval only\n    74→\n    75→### 3.2 What `C4` is not\n    76→`C4` is **not**:\n    77→- a one-shot patch only,\n    78→- a free-form search over arbitrary new strategies,\n    79→- a benchmark-hack optimizer,\n    80→- a simultaneous search over the skill *and* the refine protocol,\n    81→- or a covert shift from “skill evaluation” to “optimizer evaluation.”\n    82→\n    83→---\n    84→\n    85→## 4. Role of Pi-AutoResearch in `C4`\n    86→\n    87→Pi-AutoResearch is a natural fit for this stage, but its role must be explicit.\n    88→\n    89→### 4.1 Allowed role\n    90→In `C4`, Pi-AutoResearch acts as a:\n    91→- **bounded multi-round skill refiner**\n    92→- **failure analyst**\n    93→- **evidence integrator**\n    94→- **iterative editor under constraints**\n    95→\n    96→### 4.2 Disallowed role\n    97→In `C4`, Pi-AutoResearch does **not** act as a:\n    98→- free protocol inventor,\n    99→- open-ended benchmark search engine,\n   100→- unconstrained literature-search agent for every round,\n   101→- or refiner-of-the-refiner.\n   102→\n   103→### 4.3 Why this matters\n   104→Pi-AutoResearch may still become central to the long-term contribution.\n   105→But inside the current benchmark line it should answer:\n   106→\n   107→> “Can a fixed multi-round refine protocol improve a skill?”\n   108→\n   109→not yet:\n   110→\n   111→> “Can the system autonomously invent a better refine protocol while also optimizing the skill?”\n   112→\n   113→That second question belongs to a later outer-loop study.\n   114→\n   115→---\n   116→\n   117→## 5. Inner loop vs outer loop\n   118→\n   119→The cleanest framing is to separate two loops.\n   120→\n   121→### 5.1 Inner loop — current benchmark loop\n   122→This is the loop that produces `C4`.\n   123→\n   124→- **object being improved:** the skill artifact\n   125→- **protocol status:** fixed\n   126→- **execution style:** multi-round\n   127→- **question:** does bounded multi-round refine improve `C3` on held-out tasks?\n   128→\n   129→### 5.2 Outer loop — later research loop\n   130→This is the loop that improves the refine protocol itself.\n   131→\n   132→- **object being improved:** the refine algorithm / meta-protocol\n   133→- **protocol status:** evolving\n   134→- **question:** which refine protocol produces better refined skills with less overfitting and lower cost?\n   135→\n   136→### 5.3 Policy\n   137→Do not mix inner-loop and outer-loop claims in the same benchmark result.\n   138→\n   139→---\n   140→\n   141→## 6. Recommended round structure\n   142→\n   143→The default `C4` shape should be a bounded round sequence.\n   144→\n   145→### 6.1 Round naming\n   146→- `R0` = input `C3` skill\n   147→- `R1` = first refined candidate\n   148→- `R2` = second refined candidate\n   149→- `R3` = third refined candidate\n   150→- ...\n   151→- `C4-final` = final selected refined skill after the bounded loop ends\n   152→\n   153→### 6.2 Minimal recommended budget\n   154→For v0.1:\n   155→- default recommended range = **3 to 4 refine rounds total**\n   156→- enough to test real iterative behavior,\n   157→- not so many that the first study turns into unconstrained search.\n   158→\n   159→### 6.3 Why multiple rounds are important\n   160→Single-round refine underuses the core value of autoresearch.\n   161→Multi-round refine allows:\n   162→- diagnosis correction,\n   163→- memory accumulation,\n   164→- refinement of earlier edits,\n   165→- and better separation between noisy first reactions and more stable later improvements.\n   166→\n   167→---\n   168→\n   169→## 7. Input bundle for the loop\n   170→\n   171→A `C4` refiner should consume a structured **refine bundle**.\n   172→\n   173→The bundle should evolve round by round, but it should stay within tune-split boundaries.\n   174→\n   175→### 7.1 Required inputs\n   176→These are required to start the loop:\n   177→\n   178→#### Skill ancestry\n   179→- current `C3` skill artifact\n   180→- original `C1` skill snapshot\n   181→- if available, a short `C2 -> C3` diff summary\n   182→\n   183→#### Task context\n   184→- task instruction\n   185→- task metadata / category / difficulty\n   186→- known task constraints\n   187→\n   188→#### Tune evidence\n   189→- per-condition benchmark result summary (`C0/C1/C2/C3` or latest relevant state)\n   190→- deterministic verifier outputs\n   191→- at least one failed or weak case\n   192→- at least one successful or near-success case for contrast\n   193→- negative-transfer note when applicable\n   194→\n   195→#### Refine constraints\n   196→- allowed edit surface\n   197→- forbidden edit surface\n   198→- round budget / stopping rules\n   199→- explicit ban on held-out eval visibility\n   200→\n   201→### 7.2 Strongly recommended inputs\n   202→These are not strictly required, but should usually be present:\n   203→- suspicious-success notes\n   204→- manual audit notes\n   205→- disagreement between verifier lane and review lane\n   206→- authoring burden note\n   207→- cross-task pattern memo derived only from tune split\n   208→\n   209→### 7.3 Optional inputs\n   210→These may help later rounds but are not required in v0.1:\n   211→- previous refine memos from earlier experiments\n   212→- small frozen heuristic library\n   213→- a curated research note prepared in advance by humans\n   214→\n   215→### 7.4 Forbidden inputs\n   216→Do **not** allow:\n   217→- held-out eval examples or traces\n   218→- hidden test details\n   219→- oracle outputs\n   220→- arbitrary open-ended internet search during the refine loop\n   221→- uncontrolled prompt history from unrelated chats\n   222→\n   223→---\n   224→\n   225→## 8. Per-round memory objects\n   226→\n   227→Because this is multi-round, memory is not optional; it is the point.\n   228→\n   229→Each round should leave durable artifacts that the next round can read.\n   230→\n   231→### 8.1 Required per-round artifacts\n   232→For each round `Ri`, create:\n   233→1. `round_i_skill.md` or equivalent final artifact\n   234→2. `round_i_refine_memo.md`\n   235→3. `round_i_diff_summary.md`\n   236→4. `round_i_effect_estimate.md`\n   237→5. `round_i_risk_note.md`\n   238→\n   239→### 8.2 Refine ledger\n   240→Also maintain one cumulative ledger that records:\n   241→- what changed each round\n   242→- which evidence triggered each change\n   243→- whether the change seemed helpful, neutral, or harmful on tune evidence\n   244→- whether the same kind of edit is repeating\n   245→\n   246→This ledger is the minimum structured memory substrate for the loop.\n   247→\n   248→---\n   249→\n   250→## 9. Diagnosis categories\n   251→\n   252→The refiner should diagnose failure in a structured way rather than editing arbitrarily.\n   253→\n   254→Recommended diagnosis categories:\n   255→\n   256→1. **Trigger too broad**\n   257→   - skill fires where it should abstain\n   258→\n   259→2. **Scope unclear**\n   260→   - `scope_in` / `scope_out` boundaries are under-specified\n   261→\n   262→3. **Requirements under-specified**\n   263→   - prerequisites are missing or too weak\n   264→\n   265→4. **Risk statement too weak**\n   266→   - failure surfaces are known but not encoded clearly\n   267→\n   268→5. **Tool guidance misaligned**\n   269→   - skill nudges toward unhelpful or harmful tools/paths\n   270→\n   271→6. **Example or framing misleads**\n   272→   - examples anchor the agent toward the wrong policy\n   273→\n   274→7. **Derived layer hallucination**\n   275→   - the agent-derived expansion invented unsupported claims/constraints\n   276→\n   277→8. **Evaluator hooks too weak**\n   278→   - the skill lacks enough structure to support trustworthy checking\n   279→\n   280→9. **Body guidance too vague / too verbose**\n   281→   - the natural-language body is either too loose to help or too bloated to use\n   282→\n   283→The refiner should connect each proposed edit to one or more diagnosis classes.\n   284→\n   285→---\n   286→\n   287→## 10. Allowed edit surface\n   288→\n   289→`C4` should only change a bounded set of skill fields/components.\n   290→\n   291→### 10.1 Allowed edits\n   292→- `purpose`\n   293→- `scope_in`\n   294→- `scope_out`\n   295→- `requires`\n   296→- `preferred_tools`\n   297→- `risks`\n   298→- examples / example framing\n   299→- candidate preconditions\n   300→- candidate postconditions\n   301→- candidate failure modes\n   302→- candidate evaluator hooks\n   303→- wording changes that compress, clarify, or remove ambiguity\n   304→- deletion of clearly harmful or misleading guidance\n   305→\n   306→### 10.2 Allowed structural operations\n   307→- tighten\n   308→- clarify\n   309→- compress\n   310→- reorder\n   311→- split one overloaded rule into smaller explicit rules\n   312→- remove unsupported claims\n   313→- strengthen abstention boundaries\n   314→- strengthen anti-shortcut warnings\n   315→\n   316→### 10.3 Disallowed edits\n   317→- task-answer leakage\n   318→- benchmark-specific hacks\n   319→- hidden reliance on held-out tasks\n   320→- inventing capabilities not grounded in the task or original skill\n   321→- replacing the original task strategy with an unrelated new one unless explicitly justified and flagged\n   322→- importing large outside knowledge blocks per round without protocol approval\n   323→\n   324→---\n   325→\n   326→## 11. Multi-round refine procedure\n   327→\n   328→The loop should follow a fixed sequence each round.\n   329→\n   330→### Step 1 — Read current bundle state\n   331→Read:\n   332→- current skill version\n   333→- refine ledger\n   334→- tune evidence\n   335→- previous round memo(s)\n   336→- current constraints\n   337→\n   338→### Step 2 — Update diagnosis table\n   339→Produce or revise a diagnosis table with:\n   340→- failure type\n   341→- evidence\n   342→- suspected cause\n   343→- edit target\n   344→- confidence\n   345→\n   346→### Step 3 — Propose bounded edits\n   347→For each diagnosis item, propose edits limited to the allowed edit surface.\n   348→\n   349→### Step 4 — Produce round candidate\n   350→Generate the next round skill artifact (`R1`, `R2`, ...).\n   351→\n   352→### Step 5 — Write explainability memo\n   353→Write a per-round memo that states:\n   354→- what changed\n   355→- why it changed\n   356→- what evidence justified it\n   357→- what new risk it may introduce\n   358→- whether this round mainly tightened, clarified, or repaired\n   359→\n   360→### Step 6 — Record lineage\n   361→Store:\n   362→- parent skill version\n   363→- evidence used\n   364→- protocol version\n   365→- round index\n   366→\n   367→### Step 7 — Run tune-side check\n   368→Evaluate the round candidate only on the tune side or tune-derived evidence.\n   369→Do not peek at held-out eval tasks.\n   370→\n   371→### Step 8 — Update refine ledger\n   372→Append the round outcome to the ledger before the next round begins.\n   373→\n   374→---\n   375→\n   376→## 12. Stopping criteria\n   377→\n   378→A multi-round loop needs explicit stopping conditions.\n   379→\n   380→The loop should stop when any one of the following holds:\n   381→\n   382→### 12.1 Maximum round budget reached\n   383→For v0.1, this is expected to be small (for example 3–4 rounds).\n   384→\n   385→### 12.2 Diminishing returns\n   386→Two consecutive rounds produce no meaningful improvement on tune evidence.\n   387→\n   388→### 12.3 Harm increases\n   389→Negative transfer or suspicious-success risk gets clearly worse.\n   390→\n   391→### 12.4 Complexity inflation\n   392→The skill becomes materially heavier or less adoption-friendly without commensurate gain.\n   393→\n   394→### 12.5 Edit repetition\n   395→The refiner starts making the same type of edit repeatedly without new evidence.\n   396→\n   397→### 12.6 Confidence collapse\n   398→The diagnosis table becomes too uncertain or too contradictory to justify another round.\n   399→\n   400→---\n   401→\n   402→## 13. Selecting `C4-final`\n   403→\n   404→`C4-final` should not automatically mean “last round wins.”\n   405→\n   406→### 13.1 Candidate pool\n   407→The final selector may compare:\n   408→- `R0` (`C3`)\n   409→- `R1`\n   410→- `R2`\n   411→- `R3`\n   412→- ...\n   413→\n   414→### 13.2 Selection principle\n   415→Choose the candidate that gives the best overall tradeoff on tune evidence between:\n   416→- performance\n   417→- harm control\n   418→- reliability\n   419→- complexity / authoring burden\n   420→\n   421→### 13.3 Conservative default\n   422→If later rounds do not clearly dominate, it is acceptable to choose an earlier round as `C4-final`.\n   423→\n   424→This is another reason to treat the loop as bounded search rather than automatic “latest version is best.”\n   425→\n   426→---\n   427→\n   428→## 14. Held-out evaluation policy\n   429→\n   430→Held-out evaluation stays outside the loop.\n   431→\n   432→### 14.1 Hard rule\n   433→No held-out eval evidence should be visible during any refine round.\n   434→\n   435→### 14.2 Evaluation moment\n   436→Only after `C4-final` is selected should the system run held-out evaluation.\n   437→\n   438→### 14.3 Allowed claim\n   439→The only valid public `C4` performance claim is the held-out evaluation result of `C4-final`.\n   440→\n   441→Tune improvements are useful for search and diagnosis, but not sufficient as the final claim.\n   442→\n   443→---\n   444→\n   445→## 15. Required outputs of a `C4` run\n   446→\n   447→A proper `C4` run should create at least these artifacts:\n   448→\n   449→1. **Round artifact set**\n   450→   - per-round skill versions\n   451→   - per-round memos\n   452→   - per-round diff summaries\n   453→   - per-round risk notes\n   454→\n   455→2. **Refine ledger**\n   456→   - cumulative memory object across the loop\n   457→\n   458→3. **Final skill artifact**\n   459→   - `C4-final`\n   460→\n   461→4. **Final refine memo**\n   462→   - why this final candidate was chosen\n   463→\n   464→5. **Evidence manifest**\n   465→   - what tune evidence was used across rounds\n   466→\n   467→6. **Held-out evaluation report**\n   468→   - the only valid place to claim `C4` performance\n   469→\n   470→---\n   471→\n   472→## 16. Acceptance criteria for `C4`\n   473→\n   474→A `C4` variant should only be considered promising if it shows at least one of the following on held-out tasks:\n   475→\n   476→1. better pass rate than `C3`\n   477→2. lower negative transfer than `C3`\n   478→3. more reliable/stable behavior than `C3`\n   479→4. similar performance with meaningfully cleaner scope control or lower harm\n   480→\n   481→And it should **not** be promoted if:\n   482→- gains appear to come from benchmark exploitation,\n   483→- held-out performance drops while tune performance rises,\n   484→- harmful cases increase,\n   485→- or the refined artifact becomes much more complex without meaningful gain.\n   486→\n   487→---\n   488→\n   489→## 17. Anti-overfit safeguards\n   490→\n   491→### 17.1 Tune/eval separation is mandatory\n   492→Refine on tune tasks, judge on held-out eval tasks.\n   493→\n   494→### 17.2 No test-peeking\n   495→Held-out eval examples must not be read during refine.\n   496→\n   497→### 17.3 Fixed protocol during the run\n   498→The refine protocol itself should not mutate mid-loop.\n   499→\n   500→### 17.4 Bounded round budget\n   501→The loop must stop under explicit round and risk criteria.\n   502→\n   503→### 17.5 Preserve artifact comparability\n   504→Do not let `C4` become so different from `C3` that the story changes from “refined skill” to “new strategy package.”\n   505→\n   506→### 17.6 Require explicit evidence mapping\n   507→Every major edit should be traceable to observed tune evidence, not free invention.\n   508→\n   509→---\n   510→\n   511→## 18. Interaction with evaluator policy\n   512→\n   513→This refine protocol depends on the broader evaluator-policy document.\n   514→\n   515→In particular:\n   516→- builder / executor / evaluator separation should remain intact\n   517→- held-out evaluation should be preserved\n   518→- negative-transfer probes remain important\n   519→- suspicious successes should be flagged, not celebrated automatically\n   520→\n   521→A good refine loop is not just a score maximizer.\n   522→It is a controlled multi-round search under an anti-cheat evaluator regime.\n   523→\n   524→---\n   525→\n   526→## 19. Recommended file/artifact layout for future `C4` runs\n   527→\n   528→Suggested pattern:\n   529→\n   530→```text\n   531→experiments/skillx-skillsbench-001/\n   532→  runs/\n   533→    pilot-b/\n   534→      tune/\n   535→      eval/\n   536→      refine/\n   537→        refine_protocol_v0.1.md\n   538→        input_bundle/\n   539→          c3_skill/\n   540→          ancestry/\n   541→          task_context/\n   542→          tune_evidence/\n   543→          constraints/\n   544→        rounds/\n   545→          round-0/\n   546→          round-1/\n   547→          round-2/\n   548→          round-3/\n   549→        refine_ledger.md\n   550→        c4_final/\n   551→          SKILL.md\n   552→          final_refine_memo.md\n   553→          final_diff_summary.md\n   554→          heldout_eval_report.md\n   555→```\n   556→\n   557→The exact filenames can evolve, but the core principles should remain:\n   558→- separate tune evidence from held-out eval\n   559→- keep ancestry explicit\n   560→- make round history auditable\n   561→- preserve a cumulative memory object across the loop\n   562→\n   563→---\n   564→\n   565→## 20. Future stage: meta-protocol search\n   566→\n   567→This document does **not** answer how to optimize the refine protocol itself.\n   568→It intentionally postpones that question.\n   569→\n   570→A later project may study:\n   571→- protocol variants (`v0.1`, `v0.2`, `v0.3`)\n   572→- whether external retrieval helps refine quality\n   573→- whether memory of prior refines improves outcomes\n   574→- whether Pi-AutoResearch can improve the refine algorithm itself\n   575→- whether community-shared refine operators should become first-class MARC artifacts\n   576→\n   577→That later stage is important, but it should be framed as a distinct outer-loop research question.\n   578→\n   579→---\n   580→\n   581→## 21. Bottom line\n   582→\n   583→For the current SkillX benchmark line:\n   584→\n   585→> **Use Pi-AutoResearch to run a bounded multi-round refine loop over the skill, not to redesign the refine protocol inside the same experiment.**\n   586→\n   587→This gives us the clean first practical answer we want:\n   588→\n   589→> **Does fixed-protocol, multi-round autoresearch refine help beyond `C3`?**\n   590→\n   591→Only after that answer is visible should the refine protocol itself become the next optimization target.\n   592→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Why this document exists\n\nThe current SkillX experiment already defines:\n- `C0` — no skill\n- `C1` — original skill\n- `C2` — SkillX minimal rewrite\n- `C3` — SkillX minimal rewrite + agent-derived expansion\n- optional later `C4` — refined variant\n\nBut `C4` was previously under-specified.\n\nThe important correction is:\n\n> **`C4` should run as a multi-round autoresearch refine loop, but under a frozen refine protocol.**\n\nIn other words:\n- the **protocol** is fixed for the duration of the experiment,\n- but the **execution of that protocol** is explicitly multi-round.\n\nThis preserves both:\n- the scientific interpretability of the benchmark, and\n- the actual value proposition of autoresearch / self-refine / self-evolve style methods.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Core clarification\n\nTwo design choices were previously easy to conflate:\n\n1. **Should the refine protocol be frozen or evolving?**\n2. **Should the refine process itself be single-round or multi-round?**\n\nThese are not the same question.\n\n### 2.1 Policy for v0.1\nFor the current SkillX benchmark:\n- the **refine protocol should be frozen**\n- the **refine execution should be multi-round by default**\n\n### 2.2 Why this matters\nIf we freeze the protocol but allow multiple rounds, we still get:\n- iterative diagnosis,\n- accumulation of evidence,\n- round-to-round skill improvement,\n- and a meaningful role for memory.\n\nBut we avoid mixing in a second harder-to-interpret question:\n- whether the system is also inventing a better refine protocol while it is optimizing the skill.\n\n---\n\n## 3. What `C4` means in v0.1\n\n`C4` is:\n\n> a **bounded multi-round refinement loop** that starts from `C3`, consumes tune-split evidence, and outputs a final refined skill candidate for held-out evaluation.\n\n### 3.1 Short definition\n- **starting artifact:** `C3`\n- **refiner:** Pi-AutoResearch (or equivalent bounded refiner)\n- **execution style:** multi-round\n- **protocol status:** frozen\n- **evidence source:** tune split only\n- **evaluation claim:** held-out eval only\n\n### 3.2 What `C4` is not\n`C4` is **not**:\n- a one-shot patch only,\n- a free-form search over arbitrary new strategies,\n- a benchmark-hack optimizer,\n- a simultaneous search over the skill *and* the refine protocol,\n- or a covert shift from “skill evaluation” to “optimizer evaluation.”\n\n---\n\n## 4. Role of Pi-AutoResearch in `C4`\n\nPi-AutoResearch is a natural fit for this stage, but its role must be explicit.\n\n### 4.1 Allowed role\nIn `C4`, Pi-AutoResearch acts as a:\n- **bounded multi-round skill refiner**\n- **failure analyst**\n- **evidence integrator**\n- **iterative editor under constraints**\n\n### 4.2 Disallowed role\nIn `C4`, Pi-AutoResearch does **not** act as a:\n- free protocol inventor,\n- open-ended benchmark search engine,\n- unconstrained literature-search agent for every round,\n- or refiner-of-the-refiner.\n\n### 4.3 Why this matters\nPi-AutoResearch may still become central to the long-term contribution.\nBut inside the current benchmark line it should answer:\n\n> “Can a fixed multi-round refine protocol improve a skill?”\n\nnot yet:\n\n> “Can the system autonomously invent a better refine protocol while also optimizing the skill?”\n\nThat second question belongs to a later outer-loop study.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Inner loop vs outer loop\n\nThe cleanest framing is to separate two loops.\n\n### 5.1 Inner loop — current benchmark loop\nThis is the loop that produces `C4`.\n\n- **object being improved:** the skill artifact\n- **protocol status:** fixed\n- **execution style:** multi-round\n- **question:** does bounded multi-round refine improve `C3` on held-out tasks?\n\n### 5.2 Outer loop — later research loop\nThis is the loop that improves the refine protocol itself.\n\n- **object being improved:** the refine algorithm / meta-protocol\n- **protocol status:** evolving\n- **question:** which refine protocol produces better refined skills with less overfitting and lower cost?\n\n### 5.3 Policy\nDo not mix inner-loop and outer-loop claims in the same benchmark result.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Recommended round structure\n\nThe default `C4` shape should be a bounded round sequence.\n\n### 6.1 Round naming\n- `R0` = input `C3` skill\n- `R1` = first refined candidate\n- `R2` = second refined candidate\n- `R3` = third refined candidate\n- ...\n- `C4-final` = final selected refined skill after the bounded loop ends\n\n### 6.2 Minimal recommended budget\nFor v0.1:\n- default recommended range = **3 to 4 refine rounds total**\n- enough to test real iterative behavior,\n- not so many that the first study turns into unconstrained search.\n\n### 6.3 Why multiple rounds are important\nSingle-round refine underuses the core value of autoresearch.\nMulti-round refine allows:\n- diagnosis correction,\n- memory accumulation,\n- refinement of earlier edits,\n- and better separation between noisy first reactions and more stable later improvements.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Input bundle for the loop\n\nA `C4` refiner should consume a structured **refine bundle**.\n\nThe bundle should evolve round by round, but it should stay within tune-split boundaries.\n\n### 7.1 Required inputs\nThese are required to start the loop:\n\n#### Skill ancestry\n- current `C3` skill artifact\n- original `C1` skill snapshot\n- if available, a short `C2 -> C3` diff summary\n\n#### Task context\n- task instruction\n- task metadata / category / difficulty\n- known task constraints\n\n#### Tune evidence\n- per-condition benchmark result summary (`C0/C1/C2/C3` or latest relevant state)\n- deterministic verifier outputs\n- at least one failed or weak case\n- at least one successful or near-success case for contrast\n- negative-transfer note when applicable\n\n#### Refine constraints\n- allowed edit surface\n- forbidden edit surface\n- round budget / stopping rules\n- explicit ban on held-out eval visibility\n\n### 7.2 Strongly recommended inputs\nThese are not strictly required, but should usually be present:\n- suspicious-success notes\n- manual audit notes\n- disagreement between verifier lane and review lane\n- authoring burden note\n- cross-task pattern memo derived only from tune split\n\n### 7.3 Optional inputs\nThese may help later rounds but are not required in v0.1:\n- previous refine memos from earlier experiments\n- small frozen heuristic library\n- a curated research note prepared in advance by humans\n\n### 7.4 Forbidden inputs\nDo **not** allow:\n- held-out eval examples or traces\n- hidden test details\n- oracle outputs\n- arbitrary open-ended internet search during the refine loop\n- uncontrolled prompt history from unrelated chats\n\n---\n\n## 8. Per-round memory objects\n\nBecause this is multi-round, memory is not optional; it is the point.\n\nEach round should leave durable artifacts that the next round can read.\n\n### 8.1 Required per-round artifacts\nFor each round `Ri`, create:\n1. `round_i_skill.md` or equivalent final artifact\n2. `round_i_refine_memo.md`\n3. `round_i_diff_summary.md`\n4. `round_i_effect_estimate.md`\n5. `round_i_risk_note.md`\n\n### 8.2 Refine ledger\nAlso maintain one cumulative ledger that records:\n- what changed each round\n- which evidence triggered each change\n- whether the change seemed helpful, neutral, or harmful on tune evidence\n- whether the same kind of edit is repeating\n\nThis ledger is the minimum structured memory substrate for the loop.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Diagnosis categories\n\nThe refiner should diagnose failure in a structured way rather than editing arbitrarily.\n\nRecommended diagnosis categories:\n\n1. **Trigger too broad**\n   - skill fires where it should abstain\n\n2. **Scope unclear**\n   - `scope_in` / `scope_out` boundaries are under-specified\n\n3. **Requirements under-specified**\n   - prerequisites are missing or too weak\n\n4. **Risk statement too weak**\n   - failure surfaces are known but not encoded clearly\n\n5. **Tool guidance misaligned**\n   - skill nudges toward unhelpful or harmful tools/paths\n\n6. **Example or framing misleads**\n   - examples anchor the agent toward the wrong policy\n\n7. **Derived layer hallucination**\n   - the agent-derived expansion invented unsupported claims/constraints\n\n8. **Evaluator hooks too weak**\n   - the skill lacks enough structure to support trustworthy checking\n\n9. **Body guidance too vague / too verbose**\n   - the natural-language body is either too loose to help or too bloated to use\n\nThe refiner should connect each proposed edit to one or more diagnosis classes.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Allowed edit surface\n\n`C4` should only change a bounded set of skill fields/components.\n\n### 10.1 Allowed edits\n- `purpose`\n- `scope_in`\n- `scope_out`\n- `requires`\n- `preferred_tools`\n- `risks`\n- examples / example framing\n- candidate preconditions\n- candidate postconditions\n- candidate failure modes\n- candidate evaluator hooks\n- wording changes that compress, clarify, or remove ambiguity\n- deletion of clearly harmful or misleading guidance\n\n### 10.2 Allowed structural operations\n- tighten\n- clarify\n- compress\n- reorder\n- split one overloaded rule into smaller explicit rules\n- remove unsupported claims\n- strengthen abstention boundaries\n- strengthen anti-shortcut warnings\n\n### 10.3 Disallowed edits\n- task-answer leakage\n- benchmark-specific hacks\n- hidden reliance on held-out tasks\n- inventing capabilities not grounded in the task or original skill\n- replacing the original task strategy with an unrelated new one unless explicitly justified and flagged\n- importing large outside knowledge blocks per round without protocol approval\n\n---\n\n## 11. Multi-round refine procedure\n\nThe loop should follow a fixed sequence each round.\n\n### Step 1 — Read current bundle state\nRead:\n- current skill version\n- refine ledger\n- tune evidence\n- previous round memo(s)\n- current constraints\n\n### Step 2 — Update diagnosis table\nProduce or revise a diagnosis table with:\n- failure type\n- evidence\n- suspected cause\n- edit target\n- confidence\n\n### Step 3 — Propose bounded edits\nFor each diagnosis item, propose edits limited to the allowed edit surface.\n\n### Step 4 — Produce round candidate\nGenerate the next round skill artifact (`R1`, `R2`, ...).\n\n### Step 5 — Write explainability memo\nWrite a per-round memo that states:\n- what changed\n- why it changed\n- what evidence justified it\n- what new risk it may introduce\n- whether this round mainly tightened, clarified, or repaired\n\n### Step 6 — Record lineage\nStore:\n- parent skill version\n- evidence used\n- protocol version\n- round index\n\n### Step 7 — Run tune-side check\nEvaluate the round candidate only on the tune side or tune-derived evidence.\nDo not peek at held-out eval tasks.\n\n### Step 8 — Update refine ledger\nAppend the round outcome to the ledger before the next round begins.\n\n---\n\n## 12. Stopping criteria\n\nA multi-round loop needs explicit stopping conditions.\n\nThe loop should stop when any one of the following holds:\n\n### 12.1 Maximum round budget reached\nFor v0.1, this is expected to be small (for example 3–4 rounds).\n\n### 12.2 Diminishing returns\nTwo consecutive rounds produce no meaningful improvement on tune evidence.\n\n### 12.3 Harm increases\nNegative transfer or suspicious-success risk gets clearly worse.\n\n### 12.4 Complexity inflation\nThe skill becomes materially heavier or less adoption-friendly without commensurate gain.\n\n### 12.5 Edit repetition\nThe refiner starts making the same type of edit repeatedly without new evidence.\n\n### 12.6 Confidence collapse\nThe diagnosis table becomes too uncertain or too contradictory to justify another round.\n\n---\n\n## 13. Selecting `C4-final`\n\n`C4-final` should not automatically mean “last round wins.”\n\n### 13.1 Candidate pool\nThe final selector may compare:\n- `R0` (`C3`)\n- `R1`\n- `R2`\n- `R3`\n- ...\n\n### 13.2 Selection principle\nChoose the candidate that gives the best overall tradeoff on tune evidence between:\n- performance\n- harm control\n- reliability\n- complexity / authoring burden\n\n### 13.3 Conservative default\nIf later rounds do not clearly dominate, it is acceptable to choose an earlier round as `C4-final`.\n\nThis is another reason to treat the loop as bounded search rather than automatic “latest version is best.”\n\n---\n\n## 14. Held-out evaluation policy\n\nHeld-out evaluation stays outside the loop.\n\n### 14.1 Hard rule\nNo held-out eval evidence should be visible during any refine round.\n\n### 14.2 Evaluation moment\nOnly after `C4-final` is selected should the system run held-out evaluation.\n\n### 14.3 Allowed claim\nThe only valid public `C4` performance claim is the held-out evaluation result of `C4-final`.\n\nTune improvements are useful for search and diagnosis, but not sufficient as the final claim.\n\n---\n\n## 15. Required outputs of a `C4` run\n\nA proper `C4` run should create at least these artifacts:\n\n1. **Round artifact set**\n   - per-round skill versions\n   - per-round memos\n   - per-round diff summaries\n   - per-round risk notes\n\n2. **Refine ledger**\n   - cumulative memory object across the loop\n\n3. **Final skill artifact**\n   - `C4-final`\n\n4. **Final refine memo**\n   - why this final candidate was chosen\n\n5. **Evidence manifest**\n   - what tune evidence was used across rounds\n\n6. **Held-out evaluation report**\n   - the only valid place to claim `C4` performance\n\n---\n\n## 16. Acceptance criteria for `C4`\n\nA `C4` variant should only be considered promising if it shows at least one of the following on held-out tasks:\n\n1. better pass rate than `C3`\n2. lower negative transfer than `C3`\n3. more reliable/stable behavior than `C3`\n4. similar performance with meaningfully cleaner scope control or lower harm\n\nAnd it should **not** be promoted if:\n- gains appear to come from benchmark exploitation,\n- held-out performance drops while tune performance rises,\n- harmful cases increase,\n- or the refined artifact becomes much more complex without meaningful gain.\n\n---\n\n## 17. Anti-overfit safeguards\n\n### 17.1 Tune/eval separation is mandatory\nRefine on tune tasks, judge on held-out eval tasks.\n\n### 17.2 No test-peeking\nHeld-out eval examples must not be read during refine.\n\n### 17.3 Fixed protocol during the run\nThe refine protocol itself should not mutate mid-loop.\n\n### 17.4 Bounded round budget\nThe loop must stop under explicit round and risk criteria.\n\n### 17.5 Preserve artifact comparability\nDo not let `C4` become so different from `C3` that the story changes from “refined skill” to “new strategy package.”\n\n### 17.6 Require explicit evidence mapping\nEvery major edit should be traceable to observed tune evidence, not free invention.\n\n---\n\n## 18. Interaction with evaluator policy\n\nThis refine protocol depends on the broader evaluator-policy document.\n\nIn particular:\n- builder / executor / evaluator separation should remain intact\n- held-out evaluation should be preserved\n- negative-transfer probes remain important\n- suspicious successes should be flagged, not celebrated automatically\n\nA good refine loop is not just a score maximizer.\nIt is a controlled multi-round search under an anti-cheat evaluator regime.\n\n---\n\n## 19. Recommended file/artifact layout for future `C4` runs\n\nSuggested pattern:\n\n```text\nexperiments/skillx-skillsbench-001/\n  runs/\n    pilot-b/\n      tune/\n      eval/\n      refine/\n        refine_protocol_v0.1.md\n        input_bundle/\n          c3_skill/\n          ancestry/\n          task_context/\n          tune_evidence/\n          constraints/\n        rounds/\n          round-0/\n          round-1/\n          round-2/\n          round-3/\n        refine_ledger.md\n        c4_final/\n          SKILL.md\n          final_refine_memo.md\n          final_diff_summary.md\n          heldout_eval_report.md\n```\n\nThe exact filenames can evolve, but the core principles should remain:\n- separate tune evidence from held-out eval\n- keep ancestry explicit\n- make round history auditable\n- preserve a cumulative memory object across the loop\n\n---\n\n## 20. Future stage: meta-protocol search\n\nThis document does **not** answer how to optimize the refine protocol itself.\nIt intentionally postpones that question.\n\nA later project may study:\n- protocol variants (`v0.1`, `v0.2`, `v0.3`)\n- whether external retrieval helps refine quality\n- whether memory of prior refines improves outcomes\n- whether Pi-AutoResearch can improve the refine algorithm itself\n- whether community-shared refine operators should become first-class MARC artifacts\n\nThat later stage is important, but it should be framed as a distinct outer-loop research question.\n\n---\n\n## 21. Bottom line\n\nFor the current SkillX benchmark line:\n\n> **Use Pi-AutoResearch to run a bounded multi-round refine loop over the skill, not to redesign the refine protocol inside the same experiment.**\n\nThis gives us the clean first practical answer we want:\n\n> **Does fixed-protocol, multi-round autoresearch refine help beyond `C3`?**\n\nOnly after that answer is visible should the refine protocol itself become the next optimization target.\n","numLines":592,"startLine":1,"totalLines":592}}}

Why this document exists\n    11→\n    12→`skillx-refine-protocol-v0.1.md` defines **how** `C4` should work:\n    13→- fixed protocol,\n    14→- multi-round loop,\n    15→- tune/eval separation,\n    16→- bounded edit surface,\n    17→- round-level memory,\n    18→- held-out evaluation only at the end.\n    19→\n    20→This document defines something narrower and more operational:\n    21→\n    22→> **What exact bundle of files/artifacts should a `C4` refiner read, and what exact outputs should it write each round?**\n    23→\n    24→Without this contract, a multi-round refine loop is too underspecified to run reliably across machines, agents, or sessions.\n    25→\n    26→---\n    27→\n    28→## 2. Core principle\n    29→\n    30→For `C4 v0.1`, the refiner should be:\n    31→\n    32→> **local-evidence-first, contrastive, bounded, and auditable**\n    33→\n    34→That means:\n    35→- local execution evidence is primary,\n    36→- the refiner should see both failure and success/near-success signals,\n    37→- the allowed inputs are limited,\n    38→- and every round should leave durable artifacts.\n    39→\n    40→The refiner should **not** rely on arbitrary open-ended search during the loop.\n    41→\n    42→---\n    43→\n    44→## 3. Contract layers\n    45→\n    46→The refine bundle has three layers.\n    47→\n    48→### 3.1 Static bundle\n    49→Inputs that should stay stable across the entire loop.\n    50→\n    51→### 3.2 Round bundle\n    52→Inputs/outputs specific to each refine round.\n    53→\n    54→### 3.3 Final bundle\n    55→Artifacts needed to choose `C4-final` and evaluate it on held-out tasks.\n    56→\n    57→---\n    58→\n    59→## 4. Static bundle — required inputs\n    60→\n    61→These files must exist before the first refine round starts.\n    62→\n    63→### 4.1 Protocol reference\n    64→- `plans/skillx/skillx-refine-protocol-v0.1.md`\n    65→- this contract file itself\n    66→\n    67→These define the rules of the loop.\n    68→\n    69→### 4.2 Skill ancestry\n    70→Required:\n    71→- current `C3` skill artifact\n    72→- original `C1` skill snapshot\n    73→\n    74→Strongly recommended:\n    75→- `C2 -> C3` diff summary\n    76→- rewrite notes from earlier authoring stages\n    77→\n    78→Purpose:\n    79→- keep lineage explicit\n    80→- avoid losing the original task intent\n    81→- prevent accidental strategy drift\n    82→\n    83→### 4.3 Task context\n    84→Required:\n    85→- task instruction\n    86→- task metadata / difficulty / category\n    87→- task-level environment notes if relevant\n    88→\n    89→Purpose:\n    90→- ground refine in the real benchmark task rather than abstract skill prose alone\n    91→\n    92→### 4.4 Tune evidence summary\n    93→Required:\n    94→- condition result summary for the task or task family\n    95→- deterministic verifier outputs\n    96→- at least one failure or weak case\n    97→- at least one success or near-success case for contrast\n    98→\n    99→Purpose:\n   100→- make refine evidence-grounded instead of purely speculative\n   101→\n   102→### 4.5 Refine constraints\n   103→Required:\n   104→- allowed edit surface\n   105→- forbidden edit surface\n   106→- round budget\n   107→- stopping criteria\n   108→- explicit ban on held-out eval visibility\n   109→\n   110→Purpose:\n   111→- keep `C4` bounded and interpretable\n   112→\n   113→---\n   114→\n   115→## 5. Static bundle — strongly recommended inputs\n   116→\n   117→These are not strictly required, but in most serious runs they should be present.\n   118→\n   119→### 5.1 Negative-transfer note\n   120→Record cases where the skill appears to hurt.\n   121→\n   122→Why:\n   123→- average gain is not the only story\n   124→- SkillX explicitly cares about conditional utility and harm control\n   125→\n   126→### 5.2 Suspicious-success note\n   127→Record cases where a pass may be shallow, exploitative, or misaligned.\n   128→\n   129→Why:\n   130→- otherwise the refiner may learn to optimize evaluator blind spots\n   131→\n   132→### 5.3 Manual audit note\n   133→A human or independent evaluator summary of important non-deterministic issues.\n   134→\n   135→Why:\n   136→- deterministic verifiers often miss scope violations, misleading strategies, or shortcut behavior\n   137→\n   138→### 5.4 Authoring burden note\n   139→Record whether the skill is becoming significantly heavier, harder to maintain, or less adoption-friendly.\n   140→\n   141→Why:\n   142→- SkillX is supposed to stay lightweight by default\n   143→- cost and complexity are part of the result\n   144→\n   145→### 5.5 Cross-task pattern memo\n   146→For Pilot B or later, a tune-split-only memo summarizing repeated failure patterns across multiple tasks.\n   147→\n   148→Why:\n   149→- multi-round refine should exploit accumulated patterns, not only per-task local noise\n   150→\n   151→---\n   152→\n   153→## 6. Static bundle — optional inputs\n   154→\n   155→These are allowed, but should be treated as optional and controlled.\n   156→\n   157→### 6.1 Frozen heuristic library\n   158→A small pre-approved note of refine heuristics.\n   159→\n   160→Examples:\n   161→- tighten `scope_out` when over-activation is common\n   162→- strengthen `requires` when missing prerequisites repeatedly cause damage\n   163→- compress verbose body guidance if the agent appears not to use it\n   164→\n   165→### 6.2 Prior refine memos from other tasks\n   166→Useful only if they are clearly comparable and do not smuggle in irrelevant task-specific hacks.\n   167→\n   168→### 6.3 Curated research memo\n   169→A human-prepared short note containing high-level lessons from prior literature or internal research.\n   170→\n   171→Important:\n   172→- this should be pre-curated\n   173→- not generated by arbitrary mid-loop web search\n   174→\n   175→---\n   176→\n   177→## 7. Forbidden inputs\n   178→\n   179→The following should **not** be present in the bundle for `C4 v0.1`:\n   180→\n   181→### 7.1 Held-out eval traces or cases\n   182→Hard prohibition.\n   183→\n   184→### 7.2 Hidden test details or oracle solutions\n   185→Hard prohibition.\n   186→\n   187→### 7.3 Arbitrary open-ended internet search results during the loop\n   188→Default prohibition.\n   189→\n   190→Reason:\n   191→- this changes the problem from bounded refine to free research\n   192→- it muddies attribution and increases benchmark contamination risk\n   193→\n   194→### 7.4 Unfiltered unrelated chat history\n   195→Do not dump whole conversations into the bundle.\n   196→Only distilled, task-relevant artifacts should be used.\n   197→\n   198→### 7.5 Free protocol mutation instructions\n   199→The bundle should not instruct the refiner to redesign the protocol mid-loop.\n   200→\n   201→---\n   202→\n   203→## 8. Minimum contrastive evidence requirement\n   204→\n   205→A valid bundle should include **contrastive evidence**, not only failures.\n   206→\n   207→### 8.1 Required contrast\n   208→At minimum, the refiner should be able to compare:\n   209→- one failure / weak case\n   210→- one success / near-success case\n   211→\n   212→### 8.2 Why this matters\n   213→If the refiner only sees failure, it may over-tighten the skill and collapse its usefulness.\n   214→\n   215→Contrastive evidence helps it learn:\n   216→- what to preserve\n   217→- not only what to remove\n   218→\n   219→---\n   220→\n   221→## 9. Round bundle — per-round required inputs\n   222→\n   223→Every round `Ri` should read a round-specific bundle.\n   224→\n   225→### 9.1 Required per-round inputs\n   226→- current skill candidate (`R{i-1}` or `C3` for round 1)\n   227→- refine ledger up to the previous round\n   228→- latest tune-side result summary\n   229→- diagnosis table from previous round or current update\n   230→- active constraints\n   231→\n   232→### 9.2 Strongly recommended per-round inputs\n   233→- previous round refine memo\n   234→- previous round diff summary\n   235→- previous round risk note\n   236→- any newly added suspicious-success or negative-transfer observations\n   237→\n   238→### 9.3 Per-round rule\n   239→A later round must read the durable outputs of earlier rounds.\n   240→\n   241→This is the minimum persistence requirement that makes the loop genuinely multi-round rather than a sequence of unrelated one-shot edits.\n   242→\n   243→---\n   244→\n   245→## 10. Per-round required outputs\n   246→\n   247→Each round should emit a standard artifact set.\n   248→\n   249→### 10.1 Required outputs\n   250→For round `Ri`, write:\n   251→\n   252→1. `round_i_skill.md`\n   253→2. `round_i_refine_memo.md`\n   254→3. `round_i_diff_summary.md`\n   255→4. `round_i_effect_estimate.md`\n   256→5. `round_i_risk_note.md`\n   257→6. `round_i_diagnosis_table.md`\n   258→\n   259→### 10.2 Required content of each\n   260→\n   261→#### `round_i_skill.md`\n   262→- the actual refined skill candidate for this round\n   263→\n   264→#### `round_i_refine_memo.md`\n   265→Must include:\n   266→- what changed\n   267→- why it changed\n   268→- which evidence justified it\n   269→- what uncertainty remains\n   270→\n   271→#### `round_i_diff_summary.md`\n   272→Must include:\n   273→- field-level or section-level summary of edits from the previous round\n   274→\n   275→#### `round_i_effect_estimate.md`\n   276→Must include:\n   277→- predicted gain\n   278→- predicted harm risk\n   279→- confidence level\n   280→- whether this round mainly tightened / clarified / repaired / compressed\n   281→\n   282→#### `round_i_risk_note.md`\n   283→Must include:\n   284→- what new regressions this round might introduce\n   285→- especially over-tightening, loss of generality, or increased complexity\n   286→\n   287→#### `round_i_diagnosis_table.md`\n   288→Must include at least these columns:\n   289→- issue\n   290→- evidence\n   291→- suspected cause\n   292→- edit target\n   293→- confidence\n   294→\n   295→---\n   296→\n   297→## 11. Refine ledger contract\n   298→\n   299→The multi-round loop requires one cumulative memory object.\n   300→\n   301→### 11.1 Required ledger file\n   302→Recommended canonical path:\n   303→- `refine_ledger.md`\n   304→\n   305→### 11.2 Ledger must track\n   306→For each round:\n   307→- round number\n   308→- parent candidate\n   309→- key edits made\n   310→- evidence used\n   311→- predicted effect\n   312→- observed tune-side reaction if available\n   313→- whether the same type of edit is repeating\n   314→- whether the loop appears to be converging or drifting\n   315→\n   316→### 11.3 Why the ledger is mandatory\n   317→Without a ledger:\n   318→- the loop loses memory,\n   319→- repeated edits are harder to detect,\n   320→- and later diagnosis becomes much less trustworthy.\n   321→\n   322→---\n   323→\n   324→## 12. Bundle manifest contract\n   325→\n   326→Every refine run should have a machine-readable manifest.\n   327→\n   328→### 12.1 Suggested file\n   329→- `bundle_manifest.json`\n   330→\n   331→### 12.2 Required top-level fields\n   332→Suggested structure:\n   333→\n   334→```json\n   335→{\n   336→  \"experiment_id\": \"skillx-skillsbench-001\",\n   337→  \"run_id\": \"pilot-b-refine-001\",\n   338→  \"protocol_version\": \"skillx-refine-protocol-v0.1\",\n   339→  \"bundle_contract_version\": \"skillx-refine-bundle-contract-v0.1\",\n   340→  \"starting_artifact\": \"C3\",\n   341→  \"round_budget\": 4,\n   342→  \"heldout_eval_visible\": false,\n   343→  \"static_inputs\": {},\n   344→  \"rounds\": [],\n   345→  \"final_selection\": {}\n   346→}\n   347→```\n   348→\n   349→### 12.3 Purpose\n   350→This makes the refine run portable and auditable across machines and agents.\n   351→\n   352→---\n   353→\n   354→## 13. Final bundle — required outputs\n   355→\n   356→At the end of the loop, the refine run should produce a final bundle.\n   357→\n   358→### 13.1 Required final outputs\n   359→1. `C4-final/SKILL.md`\n   360→2. `C4-final/final_refine_memo.md`\n   361→3. `C4-final/final_diff_summary.md`\n   362→4. `C4-final/final_selection_note.md`\n   363→5. `C4-final/heldout_eval_report.md`\n   364→\n   365→### 13.2 Selection note must answer\n   366→- why this round was chosen over the other candidate rounds\n   367→- whether later rounds actually improved the artifact\n   368→- whether an earlier round was selected instead of the last one\n   369→\n   370→### 13.3 Held-out evaluation report\n   371→This is the only valid place to make the final `C4` performance claim.\n   372→\n   373→---\n   374→\n   375→## 14. Selection rule for `C4-final`\n   376→\n   377→`C4-final` should not automatically be the last round.\n   378→\n   379→### 14.1 Candidate pool\n   380→The selector may compare:\n   381→- `R0` (`C3`)\n   382→- `R1`\n   383→- `R2`\n   384→- `R3`\n   385→- ...\n   386→\n   387→### 14.2 Recommended decision criteria\n   388→Choose the candidate with the best tradeoff on tune evidence among:\n   389→- performance\n   390→- harm control\n   391→- reliability\n   392→- complexity / authoring burden\n   393→\n   394→### 14.3 Conservative rule\n   395→If later rounds do not clearly dominate, selecting an earlier round is acceptable and should be explicitly recorded.\n   396→\n   397→---\n   398→\n   399→## 15. Suggested file layout\n   400→\n   401→```text\n   402→experiments/skillx-skillsbench-001/\n   403→  runs/\n   404→    pilot-b/\n   405→      refine/\n   406→        bundle_contract_v0.1.md\n   407→        bundle_manifest.json\n   408→        static/\n   409→          ancestry/\n   410→          task_context/\n   411→          tune_evidence/\n   412→          constraints/\n   413→          audits/\n   414→        rounds/\n   415→          round-0/\n   416→            round_0_skill.md\n   417→            round_0_refine_memo.md\n   418→            round_0_diff_summary.md\n   419→            round_0_effect_estimate.md\n   420→            round_0_risk_note.md\n   421→            round_0_diagnosis_table.md\n   422→          round-1/\n   423→          round-2/\n   424→          round-3/\n   425→        refine_ledger.md\n   426→        C4-final/\n   427→          SKILL.md\n   428→          final_refine_memo.md\n   429→          final_diff_summary.md\n   430→          final_selection_note.md\n   431→          heldout_eval_report.md\n   432→```\n   433→\n   434→The exact names may change, but the contract principles should remain:\n   435→- stable static inputs\n   436→- explicit round artifacts\n   437→- cumulative ledger\n   438→- explicit final selection bundle\n   439→\n   440→---\n   441→\n   442→## 16. v0.1 operational defaults\n   443→\n   444→For the first practical use of this contract, the default assumptions should be:\n   445→\n   446→- **protocol:** frozen\n   447→- **execution style:** multi-round\n   448→- **round budget:** 3–4 rounds\n   449→- **evidence source:** tune split only\n   450→- **evaluation claim:** held-out only\n   451→- **external search during loop:** disallowed by default\n   452→- **memory object:** mandatory ledger\n   453→- **contrastive evidence:** required\n   454→\n   455→---\n   456→\n   457→## 17. Bottom line\n   458→\n   459→For `C4 v0.1`, Pi-AutoResearch should read a **bounded refine bundle**, not the whole world.\n   460→\n   461→That bundle should be:\n   462→- local-evidence-first,\n   463→- contrastive,\n   464→- tune-only,\n   465→- memory-preserving,\n   466→- and explicit about both allowed edits and forbidden information.\n   467→\n   468→This is what makes multi-round refine:\n   469→- reproducible,\n   470→- comparable,\n   471→- and scientifically interpretable.\n   472→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Static bundle — strongly recommended inputs\n\nThese are not strictly required, but in most serious runs they should be present.\n\n### 5.1 Negative-transfer note\nRecord cases where the skill appears to hurt.\n\nWhy:\n- average gain is not the only story\n- SkillX explicitly cares about conditional utility and harm control\n\n### 5.2 Suspicious-success note\nRecord cases where a pass may be shallow, exploitative, or misaligned.\n\nWhy:\n- otherwise the refiner may learn to optimize evaluator blind spots\n\n### 5.3 Manual audit note\nA human or independent evaluator summary of important non-deterministic issues.\n\nWhy:\n- deterministic verifiers often miss scope violations, misleading strategies, or shortcut behavior\n\n### 5.4 Authoring burden note\nRecord whether the skill is becoming significantly heavier, harder to maintain, or less adoption-friendly.\n\nWhy:\n- SkillX is supposed to stay lightweight by default\n- cost and complexity are part of the result\n\n### 5.5 Cross-task pattern memo\nFor Pilot B or later, a tune-split-only memo summarizing repeated failure patterns across multiple tasks.\n\nWhy:\n- multi-round refine should exploit accumulated patterns, not only per-task local noise\n\n---\n\n## 6. Static bundle — optional inputs\n\nThese are allowed, but should be treated as optional and controlled.\n\n### 6.1 Frozen heuristic library\nA small pre-approved note of refine heuristics.\n\nExamples:\n- tighten `scope_out` when over-activation is common\n- strengthen `requires` when missing prerequisites repeatedly cause damage\n- compress verbose body guidance if the agent appears not to use it\n\n### 6.2 Prior refine memos from other tasks\nUseful only if they are clearly comparable and do not smuggle in irrelevant task-specific hacks.\n\n### 6.3 Curated research memo\nA human-prepared short note containing high-level lessons from prior literature or internal research.\n\nImportant:\n- this should be pre-curated\n- not generated by arbitrary mid-loop web search\n\n---\n\n## 7. Forbidden inputs\n\nThe following should **not** be present in the bundle for `C4 v0.1`:\n\n### 7.1 Held-out eval traces or cases\nHard prohibition.\n\n### 7.2 Hidden test details or oracle solutions\nHard prohibition.\n\n### 7.3 Arbitrary open-ended internet search results during the loop\nDefault prohibition.\n\nReason:\n- this changes the problem from bounded refine to free research\n- it muddies attribution and increases benchmark contamination risk\n\n### 7.4 Unfiltered unrelated chat history\nDo not dump whole conversations into the bundle.\nOnly distilled, task-relevant artifacts should be used.\n\n### 7.5 Free protocol mutation instructions\nThe bundle should not instruct the refiner to redesign the protocol mid-loop.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Minimum contrastive evidence requirement\n\nA valid bundle should include **contrastive evidence**, not only failures.\n\n### 8.1 Required contrast\nAt minimum, the refiner should be able to compare:\n- one failure / weak case\n- one success / near-success case\n\n### 8.2 Why this matters\nIf the refiner only sees failure, it may over-tighten the skill and collapse its usefulness.\n\nContrastive evidence helps it learn:\n- what to preserve\n- not only what to remove\n\n---\n\n## 9. Round bundle — per-round required inputs\n\nEvery round `Ri` should read a round-specific bundle.\n\n### 9.1 Required per-round inputs\n- current skill candidate (`R{i-1}` or `C3` for round 1)\n- refine ledger up to the previous round\n- latest tune-side result summary\n- diagnosis table from previous round or current update\n- active constraints\n\n### 9.2 Strongly recommended per-round inputs\n- previous round refine memo\n- previous round diff summary\n- previous round risk note\n- any newly added suspicious-success or negative-transfer observations\n\n### 9.3 Per-round rule\nA later round must read the durable outputs of earlier rounds.\n\nThis is the minimum persistence requirement that makes the loop genuinely multi-round rather than a sequence of unrelated one-shot edits.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Per-round required outputs\n\nEach round should emit a standard artifact set.\n\n### 10.1 Required outputs\nFor round `Ri`, write:\n\n1. `round_i_skill.md`\n2. `round_i_refine_memo.md`\n3. `round_i_diff_summary.md`\n4. `round_i_effect_estimate.md`\n5. `round_i_risk_note.md`\n6. `round_i_diagnosis_table.md`\n\n### 10.2 Required content of each\n\n#### `round_i_skill.md`\n- the actual refined skill candidate for this round\n\n#### `round_i_refine_memo.md`\nMust include:\n- what changed\n- why it changed\n- which evidence justified it\n- what uncertainty remains\n\n#### `round_i_diff_summary.md`\nMust include:\n- field-level or section-level summary of edits from the previous round\n\n#### `round_i_effect_estimate.md`\nMust include:\n- predicted gain\n- predicted harm risk\n- confidence level\n- whether this round mainly tightened / clarified / repaired / compressed\n\n#### `round_i_risk_note.md`\nMust include:\n- what new regressions this round might introduce\n- especially over-tightening, loss of generality, or increased complexity\n\n#### `round_i_diagnosis_table.md`\nMust include at least these columns:\n- issue\n- evidence\n- suspected cause\n- edit target\n- confidence\n\n---\n\n## 11. Refine ledger contract\n\nThe multi-round loop requires one cumulative memory object.\n\n### 11.1 Required ledger file\nRecommended canonical path:\n- `refine_ledger.md`\n\n### 11.2 Ledger must track\nFor each round:\n- round number\n- parent candidate\n- key edits made\n- evidence used\n- predicted effect\n- observed tune-side reaction if available\n- whether the same type of edit is repeating\n- whether the loop appears to be converging or drifting\n\n### 11.3 Why the ledger is mandatory\nWithout a ledger:\n- the loop loses memory,\n- repeated edits are harder to detect,\n- and later diagnosis becomes much less trustworthy.\n\n---\n\n## 12. Bundle manifest contract\n\nEvery refine run should have a machine-readable manifest.\n\n### 12.1 Suggested file\n- `bundle_manifest.json`\n\n### 12.2 Required top-level fields\nSuggested structure:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"experiment_id\": \"skillx-skillsbench-001\",\n  \"run_id\": \"pilot-b-refine-001\",\n  \"protocol_version\": \"skillx-refine-protocol-v0.1\",\n  \"bundle_contract_version\": \"skillx-refine-bundle-contract-v0.1\",\n  \"starting_artifact\": \"C3\",\n  \"round_budget\": 4,\n  \"heldout_eval_visible\": false,\n  \"static_inputs\": {},\n  \"rounds\": [],\n  \"final_selection\": {}\n}\n```\n\n### 12.3 Purpose\nThis makes the refine run portable and auditable across machines and agents.\n\n---\n\n## 13. Final bundle — required outputs\n\nAt the end of the loop, the refine run should produce a final bundle.\n\n### 13.1 Required final outputs\n1. `C4-final/SKILL.md`\n2. `C4-final/final_refine_memo.md`\n3. `C4-final/final_diff_summary.md`\n4. `C4-final/final_selection_note.md`\n5. `C4-final/heldout_eval_report.md`\n\n### 13.2 Selection note must answer\n- why this round was chosen over the other candidate rounds\n- whether later rounds actually improved the artifact\n- whether an earlier round was selected instead of the last one\n\n### 13.3 Held-out evaluation report\nThis is the only valid place to make the final `C4` performance claim.\n\n---\n\n## 14. Selection rule for `C4-final`\n\n`C4-final` should not automatically be the last round.\n\n### 14.1 Candidate pool\nThe selector may compare:\n- `R0` (`C3`)\n- `R1`\n- `R2`\n- `R3`\n- ...\n\n### 14.2 Recommended decision criteria\nChoose the candidate with the best tradeoff on tune evidence among:\n- performance\n- harm control\n- reliability\n- complexity / authoring burden\n\n### 14.3 Conservative rule\nIf later rounds do not clearly dominate, selecting an earlier round is acceptable and should be explicitly recorded.\n\n---\n\n## 15. Suggested file layout\n\n```text\nexperiments/skillx-skillsbench-001/\n  runs/\n    pilot-b/\n      refine/\n        bundle_contract_v0.1.md\n        bundle_manifest.json\n        static/\n          ancestry/\n          task_context/\n          tune_evidence/\n          constraints/\n          audits/\n        rounds/\n          round-0/\n            round_0_skill.md\n            round_0_refine_memo.md\n            round_0_diff_summary.md\n            round_0_effect_estimate.md\n            round_0_risk_note.md\n            round_0_diagnosis_table.md\n          round-1/\n          round-2/\n          round-3/\n        refine_ledger.md\n        C4-final/\n          SKILL.md\n          final_refine_memo.md\n          final_diff_summary.md\n          final_selection_note.md\n          heldout_eval_report.md\n```\n\nThe exact names may change, but the contract principles should remain:\n- stable static inputs\n- explicit round artifacts\n- cumulative ledger\n- explicit final selection bundle\n\n---\n\n## 16. v0.1 operational defaults\n\nFor the first practical use of this contract, the default assumptions should be:\n\n- **protocol:** frozen\n- **execution style:** multi-round\n- **round budget:** 3–4 rounds\n- **evidence source:** tune split only\n- **evaluation claim:** held-out only\n- **external search during loop:** disallowed by default\n- **memory object:** mandatory ledger\n- **contrastive evidence:** required\n\n---\n\n## 17. Bottom line\n\nFor `C4 v0.1`, Pi-AutoResearch should read a **bounded refine bundle**, not the whole world.\n\nThat bundle should be:\n- local-evidence-first,\n- contrastive,\n- tune-only,\n- memory-preserving,\n- and explicit about both allowed edits and forbidden information.\n\nThis is what makes multi-round refine:\n- reproducible,\n- comparable,\n- and scientifically interpretable.\n","numLines":472,"startLine":1,"totalLines":472}}}

Handle duplicates, missing values, inconsistent formatting, outliers, and text processing.\n     4→skillx.scope_in: |\n     5→  - Deduplication based on logical keys and downstream requirements\n     6→  - Missing value handling (drop vs impute) based on column criticality\n     7→  - Text processing (extract numbers, clean whitespace, standardize formats)\n     8→  - Outlier handling (cap vs remove) based on statistical methods\n     9→  - Data type conversions and date parsing for time-series work\n    10→  - Ensuring referential integrity across related datasets\n    11→skillx.scope_out: |\n    12→  - Feature engineering or derived variable creation\n    13→  - Aggregation or reshaping for specific analyses (e.g., DID panel structure)\n    14→  - Statistical modeling or causal inference\n    15→  - Data validation rules beyond basic type checking\n    16→skillx.requires: |\n    17→  - pandas for dataframe operations\n    18→  - Understanding of downstream task to make informed cleaning decisions\n    19→  - Knowledge of which columns are critical vs optional\n    20→skillx.preferred_tools: |\n    21→  - `df.drop_duplicates(subset=...)` for deduplication with logical keys\n    22→  - `df.dropna(subset=...)` for critical columns\n    23→  - `df.fillna()` with median/mode for non-critical columns\n    24→  - `sklearn.impute.KNNImputer` when values can be inferred from related columns\n    25→  - `pd.to_datetime()` with error handling for date columns\n    26→  - IQR-based methods for outlier handling\n    27→  - String methods (`str.extract()`, `str.strip()`, `str.lower()`) for text cleaning\n    28→skillx.risks: |\n    29→  - Dropping too many rows harms sample size and statistical power\n    30→  - Imputing critical outcome variables or treatment indicators introduces bias\n    31→  - Removing outliers without understanding signal vs noise distorts conclusions\n    32→  - Inconsistent cleaning logic between datasets breaks joins\n    33→  - Over-cleaning removes legitimate variation needed for analysis\n    34→skillx.examples: |\n    35→  Remove duplicates by logical key:\n    36→  ```python\n    37→  df.drop_duplicates(subset=['customer_id', 'order_date'], keep='first')\n    38→  ```\n    39→\n    40→  Drop rows with missing critical identifiers:\n    41→  ```python\n    42→  df.dropna(subset=['customer_id', 'order_date'], inplace=False)\n    43→  ```\n    44→\n    45→  Impute non-critical numerical columns with median:\n    46→  ```python\n    47→  df['income'].fillna(df['income'].median(), inplace=True)\n    48→  ```\n    49→\n    50→  Cap outliers using IQR:\n    51→  ```python\n    52→  Q1, Q3 = df['amount'].quantile([0.25, 0.75])\n    53→  IQR = Q3 - Q1\n    54→  lower, upper = Q1 - 1.5*IQR, Q3 + 1.5*IQR\n    55→  df['amount'] = df['amount'].clip(lower, upper)\n    56→  ```\n    57→---\n    58→\n    59→# Guidance\n    60→\n    61→## Decision Framework\n    62→\n    63→**Deduplication**: Check for duplicates first. Examine logical structure and downstream goals:\n    64→- Survey/demographic data: one row per respondent (remove duplicate IDs)\n    65→- Transaction data: multiple transactions per user are legitimate (do NOT deduplicate by user alone)\n    66→- Use appropriate subset of columns that define uniqueness\n    67→\n    68→**Missing Value Strategy**:\n    69→1. Critical columns (IDs, dates, outcome variables): drop rows with missingness\n    70→2. Non-critical numerical: impute with median\n    71→3. Non-critical categorical: impute with mode\n    72→4. Non-critical with strong relationships to other columns: consider KNN imputation\n    73→\n    74→**Outlier Handling**:\n    75→- If sample size is large and outliers are clearly errors: remove using IQR or Z-score\n    76→- If sample size is precious or outliers might be real: cap using winsorization\n    77→- Default: 1.5 for IQR multiplier, 3.0 for Z-score\n    78→- For causal inference: be cautious about removing extreme values\n    79→\n    80→## Implementation Pattern\n    81→\n    82→1. Read and preview data (`df.head()`, `df.info()`, `df.describe()`)\n    83→2. Check for duplicates and understand their source\n    84→3. Identify missing value patterns (`df.isnull().sum()`)\n    85→4. Clean in stages: identifiers → critical fields → non-critical fields → outliers\n    86→5. Handle duplicates, missing values, inconsistent formatting, outliers, and text processing.\nskillx.scope_in: |\n  - Deduplication based on logical keys and downstream requirements\n  - Missing value handling (drop vs impute) based on column criticality\n  - Text processing (extract numbers, clean whitespace, standardize formats)\n  - Outlier handling (cap vs remove) based on statistical methods\n  - Data type conversions and date parsing for time-series work\n  - Ensuring referential integrity across related datasets\nskillx.scope_out: |\n  - Feature engineering or derived variable creation\n  - Aggregation or reshaping for specific analyses (e.g., DID panel structure)\n  - Statistical modeling or causal inference\n  - Data validation rules beyond basic type checking\nskillx.requires: |\n  - pandas for dataframe operations\n  - Understanding of downstream task to make informed cleaning decisions\n  - Knowledge of which columns are critical vs optional\nskillx.preferred_tools: |\n  - `df.drop_duplicates(subset=...)` for deduplication with logical keys\n  - `df.dropna(subset=...)` for critical columns\n  - `df.fillna()` with median/mode for non-critical columns\n  - `sklearn.impute.KNNImputer` when values can be inferred from related columns\n  - `pd.to_datetime()` with error handling for date columns\n  - IQR-based methods for outlier handling\n  - String methods (`str.extract()`, `str.strip()`, `str.lower()`) for text cleaning\nskillx.risks: |\n  - Dropping too many rows harms sample size and statistical power\n  - Imputing critical outcome variables or treatment indicators introduces bias\n  - Removing outliers without understanding signal vs noise distorts conclusions\n  - Inconsistent cleaning logic between datasets breaks joins\n  - Over-cleaning removes legitimate variation needed for analysis\nskillx.examples: |\n  Remove duplicates by logical key:\n  ```python\n  df.drop_duplicates(subset=['customer_id', 'order_date'], keep='first')\n  ```\n\n  Drop rows with missing critical identifiers:\n  ```python\n  df.dropna(subset=['customer_id', 'order_date'], inplace=False)\n  ```\n\n  Impute non-critical numerical columns with median:\n  ```python\n  df['income'].fillna(df['income'].median(), inplace=True)\n  ```\n\n  Cap outliers using IQR:\n  ```python\n  Q1, Q3 = df['amount'].quantile([0.25, 0.75])\n  IQR = Q3 - Q1\n  lower, upper = Q1 - 1.5*IQR, Q3 + 1.5*IQR\n  df['amount'] = df['amount'].clip(lower, upper)\n  ```\n---\n\n# Guidance\n\n## Decision Framework\n\n**Deduplication**: Check for duplicates first. Critical columns (IDs, dates, outcome variables): drop rows with missingness\n2. Non-critical numerical: impute with median\n3. Non-critical categorical: impute with mode\n4. Non-critical with strong relationships to other columns: consider KNN imputation\n\n**Outlier Handling**:\n- If sample size is large and outliers are clearly errors: remove using IQR or Z-score\n- If sample size is precious or outliers might be real: cap using winsorization\n- Default: 1.5 for IQR multiplier, 3.0 for Z-score\n- For causal inference: be cautious about removing extreme values\n\n## Implementation Pattern\n\n1. Read and preview data (`df.head()`, `df.info()`, `df.describe()`)\n2. Check for duplicates and understand their source\n3. Identify missing value patterns (`df.isnull().sum()`)\n4. including non-purchasers changes the question\n   106→2. **Extensive requires COMPLETE panel** (all users) - missing non-purchasers biases rates\n   107→3. **Filter to target categories BEFORE DiD** - only top-N anomalous categories\n   108→4. **Use regression, not manual calculation** - to get p-values and significance\n   109→\n   110→## Common Mistakes\n   111→\n   112→- Creating complete grid for intensive → Wrong, dilutes effects\n   113→- Only including purchasers for extensive → Wrong, can't measure adoption rates\n   114→- Analyzing all categories instead of filtering → Wastes computation\n   115→- Using 2019 as baseline instead of immediate pre-treatment → Weakens causal identification\n   116→- Not sorting drivers by magnitude → Returns arbitrary features\n   117→\n   118→## Verification Steps\n   119→\n   120→1. Examine the data's logical structure and downstream goals:\n    67→- For demographic/survey data: typically one row per respondent (duplicate Survey ResponseIDs should be removed)\n    68→- For transaction data: multiple transactions per user are legitimate (do NOT remove based on user ID alone)\n    69→- Use appropriate subset of columns that define uniqueness for the data type\n    70→\n    71→**Missing Value Strategy**:\n    72→1. Assess criticality: Will missing values in this column directly harm downstream analysis performance?\n    73→2. Assess cost: How many rows would be lost by dropping vs potential bias from imputing?\n    74→3. Decision tree:\n    75→   - Critical columns (IDs, dates, outcome variables): drop rows with missingness\n    76→   - Non-critical numerical with sufficient independence: impute with median\n    77→   - Non-critical categorical with sufficient independence: impute with mode\n    78→   - Non-critical with strong relationships to other columns: consider KNN imputation\n    79→4. Decision tree:\n    90→   - If sample size is large and outliers are clearly erroneous: remove using IQR or Z-score\n    91→   - If sample size is precious or outliers might be real: cap using winsorization (IQR method)\n    92→   - Default multiplier: 1.5 for IQR, 3.0 for Z-score\n    93→4. For causal inference work: be cautious about removing extreme values that may represent legitimate treatment effects\n    94→\n    95→## Implementation Pattern\n    96→\n    97→For complex cleaning pipelines:\n    98→1.
